text:
I did not care for this, and I should have known better than to make this in the first place when I saw the ingredients and their proportions in the recipe. I made the mistake of paying attention only to some of the 5-star reviews and not the more accurate 1-star reviews, which are VERY accurate. I agree with them completely that the mayonnaise is WAY overwhelming, Worcestershire doesn't really have a place here, the garlic is overwhelming too, and it's too thick. I tried my best to doctor it up by adding some buttermilk but, alas, the damage was already done. A horrible waste of good ingredients, particularly expensive Blue cheese. I'll stick to the one I simply throw together myself with equal parts sour cream and buttermilk,  and a LITTLE mayo. (Also, for those who are interested, salt, pepper and garlic powder to taste, a pinch of sugar, and a LITTLE splash of white vinegar)

Being a HUGE fan of blue cheese, I have made this recipe countless times- I even converted my boyfriend to blue cheese dressing instead of ranch dressing! I have tried to vary it with lower-fat items and it just didn't work- stick to the recipe and you've got a fantastic dressing. I have found that the best brand of blue cheese crumbles for this recipe is Treasure Cave, so if you can find it, try it!

text:
This recipe ROCKS!  The best blue cheese dip I have ever had!

I put in a wee bit less W. sauce (too much makes it a bit brown) than recommended, upped the garlic powder (Watch the amount of garlic powder though - once I put a bit too much in and it was dreadful!) and used quite a sharp blue cheese for my best results.

Any leftovers are "cut" with a bit of milk (for a thinner consistency) and used on salads.

text:
The best bleu (not blue, but bleu) cheese recipe I've ever tasted.  I did cut the mayo back to one cup and added a bit of buttermilk to thin.  It gave it a bit of an extra tang, but not that vinegar tang which you find with jar blue cheese "wannabe" dressings.  I add a tsp of MSG which makes the flavors "Pop" a bit.  No need to increase or "up" anything. I love serving this on an iceberg wedge with some sliced tomato.

text:
I love this and make it all the time.  It is rich, creamy and sharp because of the blue cheese.  When making dont skimp on a purchasing a good blue cheese because it makes all the difference in the world.  Also, I have read some complaints about this recipe from other reviewers.  Some state that it has too much mayo.  It does have a "mayo" taste when you first mix it all together but your not suppose to eat it right away!  Let is sit for at lease six hours, or make it the night before like I do.  Also,  yes, worchestire is in the dressing, I hate it by itself, but cant taste it when it is combined with everything.  So people quite your whinning!  Follow the directions, and let it so over night so it can work its magic.  My favorite way to eat it....with grilled jerk chicken wings:)

I don't get it! This is the BEST blue cheese dressing ever! For those of you who don't like it, I just don't understand why! Everyone has their own opinion but mine is WOW! First, you have to let this sit to "meld" the flavors. I'm not sure why people say they only taste mayo...maybe you need a better blue cheese. I also have never had this "thin out". Not sure why others did..quality of ingredients maybe? This is my recipe I have used for years! Originally called "Chart House blue cheese" from a restaurant in NYC. Flavor increases as it sets! Original recipe calls for 1/3 tsp garlic powder, which I use. I only add salt after it sits because the blue cheese can be salty.

text:
This is the original CHART HOUSE BLEU CHEESE DRESSING recipe.   I made this for years starting in the 60's then developed my own.    Personally, I use the hand blender after adding the cheese and blend smooth then add some large chunks after and stir in.   Add 1/8 to 1/4 cup milk & half n half combo to thin.   Stir in well and refrigerate overnight.  Perfect for dip or dressing.

I really hate to give a bad rating, especially when a recipe has so many 5*'s. The flavor of this recipe is good. My problem is after refrigerating 24 hrs as directed, it turned from an extremely thick dressing to thin as milk. I was so hopeful that it would have a nice dressing consistency after sitting. Especially with so many positive reviews. I've tried other blue cheese recipes from different sources and had the same result of it turning too thin after it sat. Now, why is it out of 397 reviews, as of today, only 3 other people complained that it was runny. The people that reviewed that it was too thick, could not have let it refrigerate the 24 hrs as directed. Also, how is it only 4 people had issues with it being runny. I followed this recipe as written. I really want to make my own dressing because we follow an all natural diet. I would love to find a recipe that stays creamy without being to thick or thin.

text:
This recipe is awesome!  Leave as is for a delicious and thick blue cheese dip.  For dressing, to make it pourable, I cut the mayo down to 1/2 cup and thin with buttermilk until desired consistency. For those who rated this a ONE star and say that worchestershire saw has NO business in a blue cheese dressing recipe should check out several recipes from master chefs. It's used frequently and most definitely adds alot of depth to this recipe.  HINT! If you don't have buttermilk (MUCH more yummy than regular milk), add 1 T of white or apple cider vinegar to a cup of milk. Stir lightly and watch it thicken!  I make this dressing hours ahead of time so the flavors can really meld together. Yummy!

There used to be a restaurant in town called Hartman's steakhouse. They were famous for two things: fried banana peppers, and their blue cheese dressing.  If you ordered a house salad, there was as much dressing as lettuce, and a few diced tomatoes. Add some pepper, and it was heaven. I AM THE BIGGEST BLUE CHEESE DRESSING FANATIC OUT THERE!!!  This recipe is soooooo good, so good!!!  I had to modify it a hair though!  Dont be scared to use the Worchester Sauce at all, doesnt even make it brown!  Do not use real garlic, or the whole amount unless you like it real garlicy!!!  I use about a 1/4 tsp of garlic, and it does the job just fine!  You will need to thin out the dressing a little.  Just use some milk, about a 1/8-1/4 cup will give you the best consistency!  Danish blue cheese is sooo good in it, but mix it up a little, add a little gorgonzola cheese as well!  This recipe rocks, dont change a thing, but I have tested this recipe out a couple of times before adding a review, and i think you will find this very helpful!!!  Enjoy!!!

text:
Excellent blue cheese dressing.  Be warned the recipe really does make a LOT and it is so thick that you end up with more after you thin it.  I split it in half and only put worcestershire sauce in one half because some reviewers thought it was gross in there, then we had a taste test (the next day).  In the end I added it to the other half because we liked it better with than without.  It made it just *slightly* off white, perhaps those who thought it was too strong used a tablespoon instead of a teaspoon?  I don't know, but it didn't turn *mine* brown and it was hardly apparent except for a slight salty tang.  We finished off the leftovers by dipping sliced apples into it.  That was a great late night snack.  I wish I had some now...

text:
So...I love blue cheese but I have struggled with making my own, and most of what I make I do from scratch. That said-I made it and all I could taste was mayonnaise. I was super disappointed. BUT!  Let it mellow and let the flavors meld. That super May flavor is minimized and the blue cheese flavor takes over and its amazing. Its not expensive to make. Make 1/2 of the recipe, if you are skeptical. Make it, put it in the fridge and let it work its magic. Ideally 3-4 hours I guess. THEN try it then decide if you like it. Just a couple of modifications. I add more blue cheese that the recipe calls for. I add about 4 ounces of blue cheese and put it all in a food processor and pulse it 9-10 times and then I add about 2 ounces of crumbled blue cheese and stir it in.

text:
This has been my go-to blue cheese recipe for nearly 10 years.  It has the perfect balance of flavors.  
I typically make 2 changes... first, since I love blue cheese, I use more than 4 oz. and second, the consistency of the original recipe is very dense, so that it glumps rather than spreads. I have found that adding roughly a quarter cup of buttermilk loosens it just enough, without impacting the flavor at all.

text:
I've made this recipe a number of times and agree it tends to be very thick. HOWEVER today was the best. And for those who are of the opinion that they don't like mayo my question is "are you using mayo or a 'Miracle Whip' type product?  I ask because where I've lived in recent years I've found people use the term mayo interchangeably.  Nevertheless this time I did make a few changes. First I only use BelGioioso blue cheese (it's an Italian blue cheese / Gorgonzola to be specific). I used the 4 oz. the recipe called for and blended in a blender adding a little more time 1/4 cup half and half. When I reached the consistency we prefer for salad dressing and right before removing from the blender I added an additional 2 oz. of crumbled blue cheese and just used a spoon to incorporate.   Oh regarding mayo, good mayo makes the difference try Hellmann's.

text:
Thank you for sharing your recipe.   This is by far the best tasting Blue cheese dressing I've had in a very long time.  
As for all those on here that have criticized the ingredients and the overpowering taste of mayonnaise, you're wrong.
We upped the blue cheese to 5oz. (I like blue cheese).  After we mixed the ingredients, we did as says, "let it rest covered in fridge for 24 hours".  If you were to eat it right away, it will have more of a mayo taste.  
The wife and I  would pull it out and stir it every few hours when we remembered, (just what we elected to do).  Then at the 24 hour mark, it would be a hit.

text:
I really liked this recipe but "doctored" it a little after making it many times.  I start by putting a small amount of milk in a saucepan, maybe 1/8 cup.  I then add blue cheese crumbles and melt it to a liquid.  Once cooled, I add this to the remaining ingredients, blend, add additionally blue cheese crumbles and then mix by hand.  I like my blue cheese dressing overwhemingly "blue cheesey" and this has been perfect.  You taste nothin but blue cheese and it's not as thick due to the milk.  Hope this helps!

text:
After reading negative reviews saying the mayo was overpowering, I made some changes and think I nailed it. 

Drop the mayo to a scant cup. 
Reduce the sour cream to 2/3 cup
Add in 1/4 C buttermilk and just a dash of worcestershire. I kept the mustard, garlic as directed, increased the pepper to taste. Make sure you add salt! Add pinches to your taste both before and after adding the cheese. 

I took about an ounce of the blue cheese and best it into the mayo sour cream mixture until almost smooth then folded in the rest crumbled and nto the refrigerator to meld flavours. Every few hours give it a stir. After 4 hours the flavors were spot on, it was even better the next day only needing a pinch of salt. 

Hope this helps!!

text:
I made this the other day, and it wasn't bad at all. The recipe itself has good bones, but like some people know there are alway a few tweaks needed to make something fit your own specific tastes. Next time I'd follow the recipe, but  cut the garlic powder and worcestershire  sauce down to maybe 1/2 of what is called for. I'd possibly also add a small touch of milk to make it a little more runny, and definitely use a different blue cheese, because that can alter the taste drastically. (If you live in Norway, do not use Selbu..too salty, and not sharp enough.) For those complaining that the recipe had too much mayo, I also thought the same as well when I initially made it, but after it sat for 24 hours all the flavors blended quite nice and the mayo was not overwhelming. For those saying it came out runny, perhaps you didn't follow the recipe as it was called for, used lesser quality ingredients, or perhaps you tried to substitute ingredients (light mayo, light sour cream, or yogurt), all of which can alter the consistency of something.

text:
We really enjoyed this recipe just as it is written.  Mine ended up very thick because I used homemade sourcream that is nearly as firm as a block of cream cheese.  I used regular Castello Danish Bleu Cheese crumbles from Safeway and the flavor of it was very up front and pleasant.  It is important to let it set to allow the flavors to develop.  This is especially true if you use powdered garlic instead of fresh. I use Real Mayo, not strong flavored mayo like olive oil mayo or Kraft Mayonnaise (which is salad dressing and has a completely different flavor and consistency). or you will only taste the vinegary sweet salad dressing. This did not taste like bottled dressing at all.  Those taste extremely vinegary to me. This is pleasantly mild and the primary flavors are a bit salty with garlic and bleu cheese as the main flavors.  It was served alongside Honey Chipotle wings and was a hit with my husband.  I was in a rush, but next time I will use fresh garlic in place of powdered.  Other than that, no changes.

This will be my go to bleu cheese dressing recipe from now on!

text:
I made this recipe 24 hours before and left it in the fridge. I changed it up by using equal parts mayo and sour cream (1 cup each) and deleting the Worcestershire. I also substituted prepared mustard for dry (oops!) and added about 1.5 ounces more blue cheese than the recipe called for. It came out very thick and very tasty. But incredibly rich. I may have gone overboard on the blue cheese (oops again.) But I want to address the issue some people have on the flavor and the texture. The recipe calls for blue cheese "crumbled." I'm wondering if people who are using crumbles are having issues. Cheese that comes already grated or crumbled has an additive that affects the flavor of the cheese. The wax-like substance coats the cheese and prevents you from getting the full flavor. I'm also wondering if this additive makes the dip turn runny as some people have noted. For me, I only use the brick cheese and mash it up by hand. I would make this recipe again, but I would use the amount of blue cheese called for instead of being lazy and throwing in the whole package. I might add a little lemon...

text:
I make this quite often because it tastes so good. I could eat this straight from the bowl like soup! It does not have the "chemical" taste of the bottled brands. I skip adding salt, and often add extra bleu cheese crumbles only because the bulk packages at the surplus store are of varying weights. I use only Hellman's real mayo for best results. Sometimes I thin out individual servings with a few sprays of white vinegar from a spray bottle or with milk. But most often I serve as is: super thick. I haven't bought bottled bleu cheese since I came across this recipe.

text:
I let my wife buy the ingredients at Safeway, and she does not have the same taste in blue cheese that I do.  She got some whitebread blue cheese that had almost no blue in it at all.  When I opened the container there wasn't much to smell either.  Litehouse or something like that.  Fortunately, I had a 4oz tub of blue that brought the stank, and that fixed the dressing for the most part.  I made it per the recipe first and found it very bland and uninteresting.  I would have sent it back in a restaurant.  Or dipped my fries in it.  With an additional 4oz of stanky blue it was great.  Then I added a half tsp of onion powder and really didn't find much of a difference.  It's not a BAD recipe, but I would definitely cut back the mayo to half a cup instead of 1 1/3 cups.  It's probably as good as any commercially prepared blue cheese dressings as-is, but that's not really a ringing endorsement, innit.

**I made this again recently and I still love it just as much as I did the first 359 times I made it.  I sifted through the reviews tonight out of curiosity and boredom.  I must say that the low-point reviews are so amusing and extremely transparent; transparent in the regard that if it tastes too Mayonnaisse-y, you did NOT let it sit in the fridge overnight before serving.  Do us all a favor please... If you can't follow the recipe instructions, don't put in a review.  It's not fair to those who do follow directions, to the recipe submitter, nor to the readers who have not yet tried the recipe.   It's not a truly accurate review if you haven't followed the instructions.  In this recipe, the instructions matter!!! You cannot take shortcuts on refrigeration-sit time and expect the same results as if you hadn't.  Stop being a**holes and either do it right or don't review it. Period.  

This dressing/dip is absolutely divine!!! Thank you Bill!

text:
This is a great dressing. If you mix by hand, it does need to sit in the refrigerator for at least 6 hours after you make it or it will have too much of a mayonnaise taste. If I use my food processor to mix it, I can usually eat it right away without the mayonnaise overpowering. I use it for a vegetable dip and if I am going to use it for dressing I add some milk to it and it works great. My family can not have worchestershire sauce due to dietary restrictions, so I use the same amount of lite soy sauce instead and it works great.

text:
This is an outstanding blue cheese dressing, as is. I've made it a number of times for family gatherings and everyone raves about it. I've made it in strict adherence to the recipe, but I've also made a few tweaks on accident and with great success.

I was out of dry mustard so used a mild dijon; I used 1 tablespoon. I also doubled the amount of Worcestershire sauce. Additionally, I used the refrigerated, chopped garlic in water. I used the equivalent of 1 glove of garlic plus add just a bit of garlic water. All of these changed thin out the dressing a bit, plus adds a smidge of acid to the mix.

text:
With my modifications I would give it five stars.  The amount of mayonnaise seemed way too much, so I cut it in half and substituted and equal amount of softened cream cheese. I then used my mixer to beat the mayo, sour cream, cream cheese and spices together.  I added 1/2 teaspoon onion powder and did not add any worcestershire sauce, I just didn't feel this was the place for it.  It still tasted a little too much like mayo, so I added a teaspoon of white vinegar.  I then stirred in the blue cheese (6oz).  Refridgerated for three hours.  Fantastic!  Much better than store bought.

text:
This recipe was fantastic. I admit, we were wondering "Hey, where's the buttermilk?". We had no Worcestershire sauce, so we substituted in soy sauce (at my request, I love soy sauce). We were too excited to let the dressing sit for 24 hours, and it initially tasted way too Mayonnaise-y. So we added a tiny bit of the heavy cream we had on hand, and added a lot more pepper. It was truly fantastic the next day.  Next time, I will: reduce the Mayo to about 2/3 cup, I'd add about 2/3 cup buttermilk, increase the amount of pepper, and most definitely increase the amount of the super-high-quality Roquefort we used!
